You are an expert academic assistant. Your task is to segment the following course syllabus text into a structured JSON format.
Adhere strictly to the defined modules and instructions.

### Core Modules (Always include these keys in the JSON. If no content is found for a key, use an empty string ""):
- `course_identification`: Course Number & Title (e.g., ENGL 101: Introduction to Academic Writing), Term/Semester & Credit Hours (e.g., Spring 2025, 3 credits), Meeting Days, Times & Location (e.g., MWF 10:00-10:50 AM, Room 101 or Online), Modality (In-person, Hybrid, Online Synchronous/Asynchronous).
- `instructor_information`: Instructor’s Full Name & Academic Title (e.g., Dr. Jane Doe, Associate Professor), Contact Information (institutional email, expected response time), Office Location & Hours (physical room or virtual link, scheduled weekly hours), Teaching Assistants (Names, contact, office hours/location).
- `course_description_prerequisites`: Official Course Description (from university catalog), Overview of Topics (narrative summary of core themes, key questions, subject matter), Prerequisites/Corequisites (required prior coursework, placement scores, concurrent courses).
- `learning_objectives`: Clearly stated goals describing what students should know or do upon course completion (Specific, Measurable, Attainable, Relevant, Time-bound - SMART). Use observable action verbs (e.g., analyze, compare, design, evaluate).
- `required_texts_materials`: Full bibliographic citations (Author, Title, Edition, Publisher, ISBN) for all required textbooks and readings. Distinguish required vs. recommended. Information on accessing readings (bookstore, library reserve, online links). Specifications for necessary software, hardware, lab kits, art supplies, or online platform access codes. Access to supplementary materials (lecture slides, articles via LMS).
- `course_requirements_grading_policy`: Comprehensive list of all graded components (e.g., homework, quizzes, midterms, final exam, projects, papers, participation) with their percentage weight towards the final grade. Clear definition of the grading scale (e.g., A = 90-100%). Policies for assignment submission methods, deadlines (including time zone if online), penalties for late submissions, conditions for make-up work. Statement referencing institutional honor code or academic integrity policy.
- `assignments_exams`: Descriptions of significant assignments (papers, projects, presentations) including format, length, due dates, and alignment with learning objectives. Details on major exams (midterm, final) including format (e.g., multiple-choice, essay, open/closed-book), duration, specific dates, and types of questions. Information on preparation resources (study guides, practice problems, review sessions).
- `course_schedule`: A week-by-week or session-by-session schedule, often in a table. List dates, corresponding topics, required readings, assignment due dates, and exam dates. Note any holidays or breaks when class does not meet.
- `course_policies`: Instructor's policy on class attendance (required/recommended, excused/unexcused), tardiness, and participation (in-class or online). Detailed late/missed work policy. Links to academic support (tutoring, writing centers). Universal Design & Accommodations statement (Disability Services contact and process).
- `communication_student_support`: Instructor's preferred communication methods (email, LMS messages, forum), expected response timeframe, communication etiquette. Specific links/info for Tutoring, Writing Center, Math Lab, Library Support, Counseling & Well-Being services. Campus emergency procedures contact.
- `university_wide_policies_resources`: Links/summaries of university-wide policies: FERPA (student privacy), Non-Discrimination/Title IX, Disability Accommodations (ADA/Section 504), Academic Integrity/Honor Code, Emergency Procedures/Campus Safety, IT Acceptable Use/Copyright, Grade Appeal/Grievance, Student Conduct Code, Health/Counseling/Wellness resources, Academic Calendar (add/drop deadlines).

### Optional Modules (Include these keys ONLY if relevant content is found. If no content, omit the key or use an empty string):
- `separate_laboratory_sections`: (Optional) Specific schedule & location for lab sessions. Lab Instructor/TA details. Pre-lab requirements. Lab attendance & safety (PPE) rules.
- `recitation_discussion_sections`: (Optional) Schedule & locations for recitation/discussion sections. TA details. Typical activities or topics covered. Participation policy.
- `practicum_clinical_experiences`: Extract relevant information if present.
- `field_trips_off_campus_activities`: Extract relevant information if present.
- `service_learning_community_engagement_projects`: Extract relevant information if present.
- `studio_workshop_sessions`: Extract relevant information if present.
- `performance_recital_production_requirements`: Extract relevant information if present.
- `safety_protocols_lab_attire_expanded`: Extract relevant information if present.
- `internship_fieldwork_documentation`: Extract relevant information if present.
- `emergency_health_safety_protocols_course_specific`: Extract relevant information if present.
- `ethics_controversial_content_statements`: Extract relevant information if present.

### Unclassified Content Module:
- `unclassified_content`: This MUST be a list of strings. Place any significant text blocks here that do not clearly fit into any of the defined Core or Optional modules. If all content is classified, use an empty list `[]`.

### Key Instructions:
1.  **Complete and Accurate Extraction:** Preserve all specific details: dates, times, names, locations, policies, ISBNs, links, etc.
2.  **Comprehensive Coverage:** Extract all relevant text for each module. If content seems to fit multiple modules, choose the most specific one or the one where it's most emphasized. Avoid duplicating large chunks of text across modules unless absolutely necessary for context.
3.  **Strict JSON Output:** Your entire response MUST be a single, valid JSON object. Do not include any explanatory text, comments, or markdown formatting outside the JSON structure.
4.  **Text Formatting:** Preserve original line breaks within the extracted text for each module where it aids readability (e.g., in schedules, lists of policies).

### Example:
**Input Syllabus Text Snippet:**
```text

COURSE: BIOL 202 Human Anatomy (Fall 2024)
Instructor: Dr. Eve Everyperson, Office: Bio Hall 303
Email: eeve@example.edu. Office Hours: Mon 10-12 AM.
This course covers the gross and microscopic anatomy of the human body.
Required Text: Human Anatomy, 9th Ed., by Marieb, Wilhelm, Mallatt. ISBN: 978-0134243818.
Grading: Midterm 1 (25%), Midterm 2 (25%), Final Exam (30%), Lab Reports (20%).
Schedule:
Week 1 (Aug 26): Introduction to Anatomy. Ch. 1.
Week 2 (Sep 2): Tissues. Ch. 4. HW1 due Sep 6.

```
**Expected JSON Output Snippet:**
```json

{
  "course_identification": "COURSE: BIOL 202 Human Anatomy (Fall 2024)",
  "instructor_information": "Instructor: Dr. Eve Everyperson, Office: Bio Hall 303\nEmail: eeve@example.edu. Office Hours: Mon 10-12 AM.",
  "course_description_prerequisites": "This course covers the gross and microscopic anatomy of the human body.",
  "learning_objectives": "",
  "required_texts_materials": "Required Text: Human Anatomy, 9th Ed., by Marieb, Wilhelm, Mallatt. ISBN: 978-0134243818.",
  "course_requirements_grading_policy": "Grading: Midterm 1 (25%), Midterm 2 (25%), Final Exam (30%), Lab Reports (20%).",
  "assignments_exams": "HW1 due Sep 6.",
  "course_schedule": "Schedule:\nWeek 1 (Aug 26): Introduction to Anatomy. Ch. 1.\nWeek 2 (Sep 2): Tissues. Ch. 4. HW1 due Sep 6.",
  "course_policies": "",
  "communication_student_support": "",
  "university_wide_policies_resources": "",
  "unclassified_content": []
}

```
